Summary 161:
Direct payments to farmers in the EU under the common agricultural policy (CAP) — rules for the allocation of direct payments to small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and young farmers
Direct payments in the European Union (EU)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 596/2014 — rules on the allocation and management of direct payment entitlements to small farmers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules on how EU countries allocate direct payments (i.e. payments to individual farmers) under the Common Agricultural Policy (CAP).
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out rules on:
the eligibility of eligible areas for direct payments;
the maximum amount of payments per hectare for each eligible hectare of land in each EU country;
minimum requirements for receiving direct payments.
It does not apply to certain categories of land, such as:
agriculture, forestry, fisheries, aquaculture, horticulture, forestry and fisheries;
fisheries;
seeds, fruit and vegetables;
sugar beet, cane and chicory;
fruit and vegetables and short rotation coppice.
The following categories of eligible area are excluded from the scope of the regulation:
land of less than 10,000 hectares;
horticultural land;
land with fewer than 100,000 square metres of land.
Eligible area
The number of eligible hectares is determined by using a share of the national ceiling set out in the annex to the regulation.
the number of hectares declared in each country’s national plan for the calendar year 2019 and the number declared in the region concerned for calendar year 2020.
Where an eligible area does not exceed the national cap, the EU country may decide to set a lower ceiling.
Direct payment for young farmers:
a lump sum amount per farmer calculated by multiplying a fixed number of hectare by a figure corresponding to 25 % of the average payment per hectale, as established by the EU countries;
an annual lump sum of up to €5,000 for each hectare, calculated by dividing the amount of eligible land by the number of young farmers;
a minimum amount of €10,000 per farmer, calculated as a percentage of the annual average payment.
EU countries may also decide to grant complementary national direct payments in Bulgaria and Romania.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The common agriculture policy is the cornerstone of the EU's sustainable development goal (SDP), which aims to reduce poverty and improve the quality of life of farmers and the environment.
For more information, see:
‘Direct payments’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Direct payment: a payment to a farmer for the use of his or her land. It is calculated as the sum of the difference between the total value of the payment and the total amount of land covered by that farmer.

  българска барка  грана ганка, года кандарна (OJ L 321, 1.12.2014, pp. 1-2)

Summary 163:
Road transport statistics: carriage of goods by road (Regulation (EC) No 596/2011 — carriage of traffic by road statistics (recast)
Road transport Statistics: carriage by road
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2015/849 — carriage by traffic statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It lays down rules on the transmission of statistics to the European Commission (Eurostat) on the carriage of road transport by road.
KEY POINTS
The regulation requires EU countries to compile statistical data relating to the following areas:
vehicle;
journey*;
goods.
EU countries must transmit data to Eurostat on the following:
the number of tonnes of goods transported by road;
the total tonne-kilometre of goods carried by road transport vehicles;
total number of persons travelling by road in the EU.
The data must be collected in the form of:
a list of vehicles and their registration number;
a description of the type of goods (single or main);
the type of transport (lorry or road tractor, semi-trailer, heavy goods vehicle, light goods vehicle and heavy goods vehicles);
a summary of the number and type of persons involved in the transport of goods during the journey;
an indication of the name, address or registration number of the person driving the vehicle;
details of the vehicle and of the persons accompanying the vehicle.
Annexes to the regulation specify the types of data to be collected and the methods to be used.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATED REGULATE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2015.
It repeals Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 696/2002.
BACKGROUND
 The regulation is one of a series of measures designed to modernise the EU’s statistical system.

Summary 164:
European Judicial Network in civil and commercial matters — service of documents by EU countries’ judicial officers, officials and other competent persons (EJNIC)
Eastern European Judicial Network (EjNIC): Service of documents through the EU country concerned
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1348/2000 on the establishment of an EJNic
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to establish a single European judicial network for the provision of services of documents between EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets up a single system for the transmission and receipt of documents in the European Union (EU).
It provides for:
the establishment of a single central point of contact for all EU countries in the field of judicial cooperation in civil matters (e.g. the EjNic);
the setting up of an EU-wide network of agencies responsible for providing the service of the documents referred to in the regulation;
the creation of a central register of all the EU-level agencies providing the services referred to above.
It also establishes a system of cooperation between the national judicial authorities of the EU countries which are responsible for the delivery of documents.
The European Judicial network in Civil and Commercial Matters is a network of national judicial offices, judicial officials, officials or other competent people of EU countries, which provides the information on the services provided by the agencies designated by the regulation.
Eligibility for direct service
Direct service is possible for any person interested in a judicial proceeding to effect service of a document directly through the judicial officers or officials of the country addressed, where such service is permitted under the law of that EU country.
Requests for service must be made by the addressee and the requesting agency. The requesting direct service must include:
a request for a translation or translation of the document;
a description of the nature and content of the requested document; and
a list of the persons and bodies authorised to provide the service.
A request for service may also be made via the national central register. The transmitting agency must ensure that the information requested is provided in a language easily understood by the requesting person.
If the requesting party is unable to understand the requesting service, it must provide the transmitting agency with a copy of the request and the documents of which a translation is requested.
Where the receiving agency refuses to accept a document, it may refuse to provide service or refuse to translate the request. If the applicant does not comply with the request, the applicant may ask the judge to order that the applicant be informed of the reasons for the refusal. The applicant may also ask the applicant to take any provisional or protective measures in the event of refusal.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 July 2000 and had to become law in the EU Member States by 1 July 2001.
BACKGROUND
The EJCN was set up in 1999 and is based on the Convention on the Functioning of the European System of Central Banks (COSCB).
For more information, see:
‘Direct service’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Direct service: the service provided by a judicial officer, official or other person to a person in another EU country for the purpose of obtaining a document.

Summary 165:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 on the regulation of advanced therapy medicinal products for human use and investigational medicinal products (i.e. products intended for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions)
Recognition of the benefits of biomedicine in the field of biotechnology and the use of human tissues and cells for the diagnosis, treatment and prevention of diseases
Recombination of the European Medicines Agency
Recompilation of the Medicinal Products for Human Use Regulation
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It sets out the rules for the registration, labelling and authorisation of new advanced therapy medicines* intended for use in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
tissue-based products* and somatic cell therapy* medicinal products;
combined advanced therapy products*;
immuno-therapeutic products* for the prevention, diagnosis and treatment of disease;
intravenous products* intended to be administered by a medical device or active implantable medical device.
It does not apply to products which are intended for infants, children or adults.
Tissues and cells
The products covered by the regulation are:
products which are derived from human tissues or cells;
products derived from the cells of an animal or plant;
tissues or cells derived from cells of a non-human animal;
somatic cell therapies;
medicinal products; and
surgical products.
Labelling
The labelling of these products must include the following information:
the name of the product and its intended use;
the indication of the age of the patient, if appropriate, the gender of the user;
a description of the medicinal product;
an indication of whether the product is intended for children, infants or adults;
instructions on how to use the product, including information on the safety and efficacy of the treatment;
information on the risks associated with the product.
The information must be clearly visible and clearly distinguishable from other information, such as the product’s name, the intended use and the intended age.
EU countries must ensure that these information is made available to the general public and to the European Commission, which is responsible for the implementation of the regulation.
Where an advanced therapy product is used in a hospital, institution or private practice, the hospital must establish and maintain a system for patient and product traceability.
In addition, the EU country concerned must:
ensure that the information provided by the manufacturer, importer or authorised representative is clearly identifiable;
establish and maintain an independent system for the monitoring and evaluation of the quality and safety of the products used;
assess the risks involved in the manufacture, testing, processing, preservation, storage and distribution of products and ensure that the products comply with the requirements laid down in Directive 2004/23/EC in respect of tissue and cell transplantation, and in Directive 2002/98/EC on the quality, safety and traceability of human blood and blood components.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2007 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
 
* KEY TERMS
* Advanced therapy medicinal product: a product which may fall within the definition of a tissue-based product and may be combined with other products. It may be used to treat a disease, disorder or disease.
* Medication: a substance that is administered by means of a central or sub-specialised medical device and is intended to prevent, diagnose, treat or alleviate the symptoms of a disease or disease or to prevent or treat the effects of disease or a disease in the body. It does not replace, cure or alleviate symptoms of the disease or disorder, but is intended only to reduce the risk of its occurrence or to reduce its duration of use.
ACT
Regulation 2006/96/EC of the Council and of the Representatives of the Governments of the Member States, meeting within the Council of 11 December 2006 on the Regulation on the Registration, Labelling and Authorisation of Advanced Therapy Medicines for human Use and Investigational Medicines (i) (OJ L 168, 15.12.2006, pp. 1-8)

Summary 166:
Emissions from motor vehicles — type approval and type-approval procedures for motor vehicles and their trailers (until 2 January 2020)
Expiry of the type approval of motor vehicles: type approval, type-certificates of conformity and type certification
Exemptions from type approval
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2008 — type-approved motor vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for type approval (EC type approval) and type certificates (NACs) for the sale, registration and operation of vehicles in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Type approval
The regulation applies to motor vehicles with a mass not exceeding 2.5 tonnes and a gross tonnage not exceeding 10,000 kg.
Types of vehicles covered by the regulation are:
motor vehicles designed and built for the transport of goods by road;
vehicles intended and built to carry passengers;
cars and light commercial vehicles intended for passenger transport;
categories of vehicles intended to be driven by passengers, such as ambulances, fire engines, ambulances and ambulances;
trams and coaches;
light commercial vehicles.
Manufacturers’ type approval obligations
The manufacturer of a motor vehicle must apply for EC type approval or national type approval to the competent authority in the EU country in which the vehicle is registered.
The competent authority decides whether the vehicle meets the requirements of the regulation.
If the vehicle manufacturer does not meet the requirements, the manufacturer is required to submit a certificate of conformity assessment (CCA).
The certificate is issued by the competent national authority and is valid for 10 years after the vehicle has been approved.
Certificates
The CE type certificates are issued by national authorities and are valid for a maximum period of 10 years from the date of application for CE type approval.
National authorities must ensure that the CE type certificate is valid throughout the EU and that the vehicle complies with the requirements laid down in the regulation and that it is accompanied by the CE conformity assessment certificate.
Type-certificate of conformity
If a vehicle does not comply with the regulation’s requirements, it is subject to CE type certification and may be subject to a number of penalties, including:
a ban on the sale of the vehicle;
a prohibition on the placing on the market or putting into service of a vehicle which is likely to cause serious injury or damage to the health or safety of persons or property;
restrictions on access to vehicle repair and maintenance information and to the information relating to vehicle maintenance.
EU countries must also ensure that:
vehicle owners and operators have the right to:
access to vehicle information;
information relating to the type of vehicle and to its maintenance and repair; and
information concerning the type and number of types of vehicles registered in their country.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGUMENT APPLY?
 
   
It has applied since 2 January 2008. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 2 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
* Motor vehicle: a vehicle with at least 2 different energy converters and two different energy storage systems (e.g. a hybrid vehicle).
* Light commercial vehicle: any vehicle intended for transport by road or by rail, whether or not it is propelled by a motor engine or by a combination of internal combustion engines.
* Heavy commercial vehicles: vehicles designed to transport goods and having a gross mass of more than 2,500 kg and which are propelled by at least one engine and have a gross weight of at least 1,700 kg and are not propelled by more than one engine.
ACT
  барсканка грандан гарка, гъланна брака  годанъка and глаксана  харганика (OJ L 183, 28.7.2008, pp. 1-2)

Summary 167:
Risk assessment of substances in foodstuffs: EU list of substances
Risk Assessment procedure for substances in foods
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 596/2013 on the EU’s system of risk assessment in matters of food safety
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a system of EU-wide risk assessment procedures for the placing on the market of substances* in the food chain.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all substances in the EU which are listed in Annex I to Regulation (EC) No 178/2002 (see summary).
It does not apply to:
foodstuffs intended for human consumption;
foods intended for sale to the general public;
medicinal products intended for use by the general population; or
food and feed intended for infants and young children.
The list is updated by the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA).
The European Commission is responsible for updating the list.
It must consult the European Medicines Agency (EMSA) and other relevant bodies in order to obtain the information it needs to make an informed decision.
Amendments
Amending Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/856 introduces a new procedure for the updating of the EU list. It allows the Commission to adopt implementing measures to ensure the consistency of the list with the EU countries’ national lists.
Implementing measures are adopted by the Commission within 6 months of the date of entry into force of each sectoral food law.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY TO APPLY?
From 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU lists of substances are published in the Official Journal of the European Union (OJ).
For more information, see:
‘Food safety’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Substances: substances used in food or in food preparation, storage, transport, storage and distribution.
ACT
Council Regulation (Euratom) No 550/2013 of 20 December 2013 on the system of risks assessment in the field of food and in matters relating to food safety (recast).

Summary 168:
Accreditation, market surveillance and market surveillance of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (until 2023)
Assessment of conformity assessment bodies and accreditation of products entering the European Union (EU)
As part of the EU’s effort to modernise its internal market, the European Commission has drawn up a framework for the accreditation, surveillance and control of products coming into the EU from outside the EU.
ACT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 596/2008 of 25 June 2008 laying down rules for the application of Regulation (EEC) No 1605/2002 of the European Parliament and of the Council relating to accreditation and the market surveillance framework.
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It lays down rules on accreditation*, market surveillance* and controls of products imported from non–EU countries.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the conditions under which accreditation* is granted to a national conformity assessment body (NCB) to assess whether a product meets the essential requirements of EU legislation.
Accreditation is the process by which an accreditation body attests to the conformity of a product to the relevant legislation. It is carried out by a body designated by an EU country.
Each EU country appoints one or more national accreditation bodies to carry out the assessment.
The accreditation process is based on a set of principles:
non-discrimination;
the body is independent of the assessment bodies it assesses;
there are no conflicts of interest between the bodies;
it is transparent and non-discriminatory;
conformity assessment procedures are carried out in line with EU legislation;
accreditation bodies are independent of any commercial pressures;
they are not involved in the decision-making process.
WHEN DOES THE RECOMMARKET SURVEILLANCE FRAMEWORK AND CONTROL OF PRODUCTS ENTER INTO THE COMMUNITY MARKET APPLY?
From 1 January 2010, the regulation applies to all products that are released for free circulation in the EU, whether they are new or second hand.
It does not apply to:
new products that have not been accredited;
products that have been placed on the market for the first time;
pre-existing products which have been withdrawn from the market or are prohibited or restricted.

Summary 169:
Agreement between the EU and Iceland on mutual recognition of arrest warrant and extradition procedures (MRA/EEC)
Agreement with Iceland on Mutual Recognition of Arrest Warrant and Extradition Procedures (MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision 2008/852/EC of 26 June 2008 on the conclusion of the Agreement between the European Union and the Kingdom of Norway and the Republic of Iceland on the mutual recognition and extradition of arrest warrants and the mutual extradition procedures between the Member States concerned
Agreed Framework Decision (EU/Iceland) 2016/848 on the signing, on behalf of the EU, and provisional application of the Agreements between the Community and its Member States on mutual Recognition and Interoperability with respect to Arrest Warrant Agreements and the Extraditable Arrangements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to facilitate the arrest and subsequent extradition of persons who are wanted for criminal offences in the EU.
The decision concludes the agreement with Iceland.
KEY POINTS
Iceland and the EU agree to:
cooperate in the execution of an arrest warrant issued by an EU country against an individual who is suspected or suspected of committing an offence in another EU country;
ensure that the person concerned is held responsible for the acts for which the warrant has been issued;
implement a mutual recognition system between the two parties, in order to ensure that the arrest warrant is carried out in accordance with the law of the country concerned;
inform each other of the reasons for non-execution of the warrant.
In addition, the agreement provides for:
a mutual recognition mechanism between the parties;
the possibility for each party to request the other party to execute the warrant if it considers that the requested person is a threat to national security or public order;
an obligation on the requesting party to cooperate with the executing party in the event of multiple requests.
Amendments to the agreement
In 2016, the parties agreed to extend the agreement’s period of entry into force by 5 years from the date of its signing.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Agreement entered into force on 1 July 2016.
BACKGROUND

EU-Iceland mutual recognition agreement (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Arrest warrant: an international warrant issued for the arrest of a person for an offence which is punishable by a maximum sentence of imprisonment of at least 5 years.

Summary 170:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 on the carriage of passengers on rail passenger services
Regulation(EU) No 550/2006 — carriage charge and passenger rights
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It lays down common rules for the carriage charge* and the passenger rights relating to passenger carriage on railway passenger services in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all passengers travelling by rail in the EU.
It does not apply to:
travel information and reservation systems;
carriage charges;
the carriage of goods by rail;
traffic management and ticketing procedures;
ticketing procedures.
Passengers have the right to make a claim for compensation if:
they are the subject of a loss or damage claim;
their travel pass or season ticket is invalid or has expired;
they do not have a valid travel pass; or
their carriage is delayed or cancelled.
The carriage charge is calculated in accordance with the following principles:
the carrier is liable for the entire cost of the carriage;
it is based on the number of passengers and the total number of persons in the carriage.
Carriage charges are calculated on the basis of:
a passenger’s number of travel days;
an average number of journeys per day; and
the number of people travelling per day.
If a passenger is not entitled to compensation, the carrier is responsible for the full or partial payment of all the carriage charges.
Claims
The following types of claim may be made:
including:
claims for loss of a travel pass, a season ticket or a travel ticket;
claim for damage or loss of an item of luggage;
a claim for damage to a property, such as damage to an object, damage to property, loss or destruction of a vehicle, loss of goods or damage to personal property.
A claim may also be made for:
loss or damage of goods and services;
damage to a vehicle;
loss of a person or goods belonging to a person belonging to the same person;
damaged or destroyed property belonging to one of the persons entitled;
losing or damaging an item belonging to an individual belonging to another person.
Where a claim is made by a passenger, the person entitled must:
make a claim within 12 months of his/her becoming aware of the loss of the item;
be informed of the carrier to whom the claim is addressed;
notify the carrier of the name and address of the person who made the claim, and the person to whom it is addressed.
In addition, the passenger must be informed of any other measures taken by the railway undertaking to deal with a claim.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
 
   
It has applied since 1 January 2007.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
* Passenger rights: the right of passengers to have their travel ticket or travel pass cancelled or delayed.
* Carriage charge: the amount of money charged by a railway undertaking for carriage of a passenger from the place of purchase to the place where the carriage is to be delivered.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  (EU) 2016/596 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2016 on the common carriage charge (recast) (OJ L 347, 12.12.2016, pp. 1-8)

Summary 171:
EU statistics on education, training and lifelong learning: statistical production and transmission
EU statistics about education and training
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2008 on the production of specific statistics on Education, Training and Lifelong Learning
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to improve the quality and reliability of European Union (EU) statistics in the field of education, learning, lifelong learning and vocational training.
It lays down the rules for the production, transmission and dissemination of statistics in these fields.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries and the European Commission (Eurostat).
It does not apply to:
the EU countries’ national statistics institutes;
the European Statistical System of Europe (ESSE);
the statistical units (e.g. Eurostat); and
the statistics produced by Eurostat.
Data transmission
Eurostat must transmit confidential micro-data resulting from sample surveys to the Commission, subject to confidentiality, in accordance with the provisions on the transmission of data.
EU countries must ensure that the transmitted data do not permit the direct identification of the statistics units (individuals).
The Commission must transmit the data to Eurostat in the format set out in the annex to the regulation.
The data must be transmitted in a language easily understood by the EU countries, in a format that is consistent with the EU’s common statistical system.
In addition, EU countries must transmit information on:
a list of the variables to be used for the compilation of statistics
the list of variables and their codification
the definitions of those variables
the names of the statistical units
the definition of the categories of data to which the data relate
the classification of the data
the categories of information to be transmitted by EU countries
the types of statistical units to be produced
the data to be made available for the purposes of the compilation and interpretation of comparable statistics.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
From 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to modernise and modernise the EU statistics system. These include:
Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2019/1369, which sets out the conditions for the establishment of an integrated European statistical information system on education (see summary);
Regulating (EU), Euratom, EEC and EFTA countries (EC, EFTA and the EEA) 2018/856, which set out the criteria for the creation of the European Statistical Information System (ESIS), which is based on a framework of coherent concepts and comparable data in view of the development of a common European statistical knowledge base.
For more information, see:
‘Education and training statistics’ on Eurostat's website.

Summary 172:
EU energy statistics: energy consumption
EU energy consumption: energy statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 596/2008 — energy statistics (energy statistics)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the transmission and dissemination of energy statistics to the European Commission and the European Energy Agency (EEA).
It aims to improve the quality and comparability of EU energy statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries and to the EU countries’ Member States, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland and the Faroe Islands.
It does not apply to Denmark, Greenland, the Azores and Madeira.
EU countries must provide the Commission with:
energy consumption statistics for the period 1 January to 31 December of each calendar year;
energy stocks* for each month of the year.
Reporting
The Commission must publish energy statistics in a format that is consistent with the EU’s national legislation.
Energy statistics must be based on:
the following sources of energy;
the sources and methods used to compile the statistics; and
the information they contain.
Transmission and dissemination
Each year, the Commission publishes a report on the energy consumption statistics it receives from the Member States and the EEA Member States.
The report must be published in the Official Journal of the European Union (OJ). It must contain the following information, including:
a list of energy sources and types of energy used;
a description of the sources and technologies used to produce the energy statistics;
an indication of the types and quantities of energy products and fuels used in each type of energy production and consumption;
information on the production and use of electricity and energy storage;
statistics on the generation, transmission and consumption of electricity;
data on energy storage and distribution of electricity, including a breakdown of electricity stocks;
gas consumption statistics, including gas consumption and LNG consumption.
In addition, the report must contain information on the following categories of energy:
total energy production;
total electricity generation;
electricity stocks; and stocks of electricity.
Electricity production
Total electricity generation
Total production of electricity: electricity produced by electricity plants and electricity stored in the form of electricity mains power plants (i.e. power plants that are not connected to the grid).
Total consumption
Total energy consumed by electricity: total energy consumed in the electricity generation and distribution sector.
Total generation of electricity (including electricity storage): total energy used in electricity generation, electricity storage and electricity distribution.
Emissions of energy
Total emissions of energy from energy generation, including electricity storage, electricity distribution and electricity consumption: total electricity produced, electricity stored, electricity exported, electricity imported and electricity exported.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EEU) No 550/2008 of 29 June 2008 on energy statistics and repealing Regulation (EC) no 594/2006 (OJR) (OJC L 347, 30.12.2008, pp. 1-8)

Summary 173:
Rights of disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility when travelling by bus or coach (Regulation (EC) No 596/2004)
Rights and obligations of passengers when travelling on public transport
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2016/852 — passenger rights and obligations relating to the carriage of passengers by bus and coach
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out a common set of rights for passengers travelling by public transport in the European Union (EU).
It aims to ensure equal treatment of all passengers, irrespective of their physical, mental or social disability.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
bus and coach passengers, regardless of their age, disability or reduced mobility;
passengers in wheelchairs and other mobility equipment;
persons who are blind or partially sighted;
people who are visually impaired.
It does not apply to passengers who are physically handicapped.
Passenger rights
Passengers have a number of rights, including:
the right to transport within the EU, including the right to use the means of transport, such as lifts, escalators and escalators, and to be assisted by a qualified person;
access to information and assistance, including first aid, accommodation, food, clothes and transport.
The right to travel without undue delay or cancellation of a regular service, including a right to re-routing or reimbursement of the ticket price.
Right to travel in a coach or a bus without delay, without being accompanied by a person in a wheelchair or a person using a mobility device.
Access to information, accommodation and transport, including access to transport information, including information on accessibility, and access to services, including assistance with mobility equipment.
Transport contract
The passenger is the weaker party to the transport contract, and therefore is entitled to a minimum level of protection. However, the passenger is not entitled to compensation for any loss or damage caused to the vehicle or infrastructure.
Compensation in respect of wheelchairs, mobility devices and mobility equipment
The carrier is obliged to compensate for any damage or loss caused to wheelchairs or mobility devices or devices used by passengers. The amount of compensation must be calculated according to applicable national law.
In addition, the carrier is required to provide passengers with:
information on passenger rights in a language easily understood by all passengers;
transport information in an accessible format;
refunds or continuation of the regular service if the service is cancelled or delayed in departure for more than 120 minutes;
reimbursement of any ticket price if the ticket is not valid.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2017. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Passenger: any person who is physically, mentally or socially disabled and has reduced mobility.
* Carriage: a vehicle or a service operated by a transport company or a private company for the purpose of transporting passengers by road, rail, sea, air or other means.

Summary 174:
Statistics on the structure of the aquaculture sector (2008-2020)
Statistics on:
the structure and characteristics of the EU’s aquaulture sector
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2008 — statistics on the aquaiculture sector
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It aims to provide EU countries with reliable, comparable and up-to-date statistical information on the production and development of the European Aquaculture (AAS) sector.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the EU countries’ participation in the aquaquaculture activities conducted in freshwater and saltwater on their territory. It does not apply to fish, crustaceans and molluscs, lakes and other waters other than those used by the EU.
EU countries must:
use surveys or other statistically validated methods covering at least 90 % of the total production by volume;
use the methods set out in the annexes to the regulation;
ensure that the data are collected and compiled within 12 months of the end of the reference calendar year;
provide the data to Eurostat, the European Commission, which is assisted by the Standing Committee for Agricultural Statistics.
The data are to be used for the following purposes:
assessing the structure and the characteristics of each part of the sector;
collecting, analysing and compiling the statistics;
checking the quality of the data;
analyzing the data.
Compilation and transmission of the statistics.
Annexes to this regulation are as follows:
Aquaculture statistics:
Each year, EU countries must submit a report to the Commission (Eurostat) on the statistics they have collected and the data they have compiled.
Each report must include:
a description of the methods used to collect the data (e.g. postal questionnaires, personal interviews, censuses or sampling, frequency of surveys, estimation methods);
the number of fish and crustacean species produced;
the total number of tonnes of each species;
a list of the types of facilities used;
data on the number and types of aquatic plants used; and
a summary of how the statistics are processed and compiled and how long this takes.
In addition, the Commission must submit an evaluation report every 3 years to the European Parliament and to the Council on the data compiled pursuant to this Regulation and, in particular, on their relevance and quality.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The Regulation entered into force on 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
Fisheries statistics
For more information, see:
‘Fishery statistics’ on Eurostat's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Fishing: the catch and consumption of fish (including eggs) by land, sea and air, including fish caught in fresh water, saltwater, lakes, other waters and other water other than the EU, including the fishing of fish by sea, air and land.

Summary 175:
Convention Area for the Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources (CAC) (see summary)
Convention area for the conservation and management of fishery resources (Cac)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1224/2009 on the implementation of the Convention Area for Community Fisheries and the CAC
Decision (EU) 2017/849 on the application of the convention area for Community fisheries and of the Cac Convention to the EU
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND OF THE DECISION?
The regulation establishes the Cascadia Convention Area, which aims to prevent and combat illegal fishing and the illegal taking of fish by vessels flying the flag of non-signatory countries.
The decision adopts the regulation on behalf of the European Community (now the EU).
KEY POINTS
The convention area is defined by the International Convention on the Conservation of Atlantic Tunas (ICCAT), which was signed by all the signatory countries in 1979. It covers the fishing waters of the Atlantic Ocean, including the exclusive economic zone (EEZ), which is defined as the sea between the coasts of the EU and the Gulf of Mexico, and includes all fishing vessels of the following countries:
the EU;
non-EU countries;
the United Nations Economic Commission for Europe (UNECE);
the World Trade Organization (WTO); and
the International Maritime Organization (IMO).
The EU is a contracting party to the ICCAT.
It is responsible for implementing the convention and for ensuring that non-member countries comply with its rules.
Catchings and identifications are carried out under the auspices of the Nomenclature of Fisheries and Aquaculture of the Faroes (NEAFCFishery Management Scheme).
Inspections
Each signatory country must designate a competent authority to carry out inspections of vessels flying its flag in the area covered by the convention. This authority is designated by the Commission or by the body designated by it.
Each country must ensure that an inspection vessel is present during that time in the regulatory area or that an agreement has been concluded with another country to ensure the presence of such a vessel.
If a vessel is not called to port, the flag EU country must provide due justification in a timely manner to the Commission and the body by that flag country for a thorough inspection under its authority.
Every inspection must be documented by the completion of an inspection report using the form established in accordance with Article 50(2) of the regulation. The report must include, where appropriate, the number of fishing days and the catch taken in the fishing area since the start of fishing, or since the last catch report;reports on the quantities on-loaded and off-loaded for each transhipment of fish during the vessel’s stay in the REGION Area.
Reports on non-contracting parties activities
Reports must be sent to the NEAFC Secretary, who forwards the information promptly to the European Commission, which forwards it to the competent national authority of the country in which the vessel is registered. The Commission then forwards this information to the NCAF Secretary, which then forwards it, in turn, to the relevant national authority in the Member State in which it is registered, and to the United Nations Environment Programme (UNEP).
If an inspection is carried out by an EU country, it must transmit the results of the inspection, as well as the information on the vessel and the fishing vessel, to: the Commission;the NCAFC Secretary;the UNECE Secretariat;the Commission or the body in charge of fisheries and aquaculture;the International Commission for the Prohibition of Unlawful Trade in Fishing Vessels (ICPN) and the International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRN);the International Labour Organization (ILO); andthe World Health Organization (WHO).
Monitoring and enforcement
The following measures must be taken:
inspections must be carried out at least once a year;
if an infringement is found, the vessel must be brought to the attention of the competent authority and informed of the reasons for the infringement;
a penalty must be imposed for infringements of the above.
EU countries must take all necessary measures to ensure that vessels flying their flag are subject to the control and enforcement measures laid down in this regulation.
In addition to surveillance reports and information on inspections, Member States may at any time submit any further information which might be relevant for the identification of vessels that might be carrying out IUU activities in the Convention area.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS APPLY?
 
   
The regulations have applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
The Convention provides for an appropriate framework for multilateral cooperation on the rational conservation and sustainable management of fisheries.
For more information, see:
Fishing in the Atlantic (European Commission).

Summary 176:
Ecolabeling of food and feed
Ecolabelling of foods and feed products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on the European Union Ecolabel
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets out the rules for the setting of ecodesign* requirements for products intended for human consumption.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all food, feed and animal feed intended for sale in the EU.
It does not apply to:
products intended for the production, storage, transport, storage or disposal of food or feed;
food and feed intended to be fed to animals or domestic animals;
animal feed intended exclusively for consumption by animals and domestic animals.
Requirements
Products covered by the regulation must comply with the following requirements:
be safe and ecodegradable;
not contain substances that present a risk to human health or the environment;
have a minimum energy consumption of no more than 0.5 kW/kg of energy per unit of volume;
be manufactured in a way that minimises the environmental impact of the product on the environment and human health;
use only products that are safe and environmentally sound.
Eligibility
Products are subject to the following conditions:
they must meet the requirements laid down in Regulation (EC) No 1980/2000 on energy efficiency (see summary);
they are not intended for direct sale to the general public;
they do not contain substances with a potential harmful effect on human health and the environment (e.g. food or animal feed);
the product group criteria are set out in Annex I of the regulation.
Products which meet all of these requirements are eligible for the EU Ecolabelled status.
The European Commission is assisted by a Committee which is composed of representatives of the Member States and is chaired by the Commission. It is responsible for:
monitoring compliance with the criteria;
assessing the suitability of products to meet the criteria and assessing their suitability for use;
making recommendations to the Commission;
advising the Commission on how to improve the application of the criteria.
Application procedure
An application procedure is established for each product to be designated as an EU ecolabel by the competent body of an EU Member State. The application procedure consists of the following steps:
the applicant must submit a product application to the competent authority in the Member State in which the product is to be placed on the market;
the competent body assesses the product to determine whether it complies with the requirements and issues a registration number to the product.
If the product meets all of the requirements, it is awarded an EU EColabel. The competent body then transmits the registration number and, if necessary, a CE marking to the manufacturer or importer.
Once the CE marking has been assigned, the manufacturer, importer or authorised representative of the importer must ensure that the product bears the CE mark and that it is accompanied by the appropriate documentation. If the product does not comply with these requirements, the product may be withdrawn from the market or withdrawn from circulation.
Certification of compliance
The competent body must verify that a product meets the requirements by carrying out a risk assessment and by issuing a CE mark or CE marking. The CE marking is valid for 10 years and may be renewed if the product has not been used for more than 10 years.
Where a product is withdrawn from use, the holder is liable for any damage caused to the environment caused by the withdrawal of the CE label or the loss of its CE mark.
Registration
The product is registered in the territory of the EU and must be accompanied by a certificate issued by a competent body in accordance with the rules laid down by the Regulation (EU).
The CE marking must be affixed on the product by the end of the 10-year validity period.
Labels and registration number
A product must bear the following information on its label or registration number:
a description of the nature and characteristics of the products concerned;
an indication of the type of product;
a list of authorised importers, importers and authorised representatives of importers; and
the name and postal address of the authorised importer/expiry date.
An optional label with text box (the possibility for the operator to use this text box and the text used shall be that specified in the relevant product category) must also be attached to a product, provided that it does not contain any other information other than the information specified in Annex II to the regulation, and that the label is clearly visible to the end consumer.
Regulatory procedure
The Commission adopts the criteria for the establishment of the European Commission’s delegated authority, the European Environment Agency (EEA), and the Commission, assisted by the EEA, and adopts an implementing act. The Commission may adopt delegated acts in the light of public consultation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE



Summary 177:
Protection of medicinal products protected by a patent
Protection against counterfeiting — granting a certificate to protect medicinal products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2006 — granting certificates for the protection of medicines protected by patents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that patents granted by the European Patent Office (EPO) are protected by certificates issued by national authorities.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (Euratom) No 1082/91.
KEY POINTS
Protected products are those products which are the result of long, costly research and which are subject to patent protection.
The protection granted by a certificate is limited to the product covered by the authorisation to place the product on the market as a medicinal product. It does not extend to the products covered by a basic patent.
Licence to manufacture a protected product is granted to the holder of a patent. A certificate may be granted for a product protected by an EPO if it is:
the result of a long-term research programme;
the subject of an application for a patent; or
the product to which the patent relates.
Certificates are valid for a maximum period of 20 years. They may be renewed for an additional period of 5 years if the product is protected by another patent, or for an indefinite period if the term of protection is reduced by the number of years of the patent. The period of validity of the certificate is determined by national law.
Application for a certificate
An application for protection must contain the following information:
a description of the nature and nature of the protected product;
a copy of the original patent;
an application for an extension of the duration of the protection granted to a protected by the EPO; and
the number and date of the first authorisation issued by the EU country in which the product was obtained.
If the application is rejected, the applicant must provide all the information set out in the annex to the regulation, including the name and address of the competent national authority, the date of application for the certificate and the number and number of authorisations granted.
A certificate is valid for 10 years, unless it is renewed for a further 5 years.
Duration of protection
The duration of a certificate may not be shorter than the period of protection conferred by the patent, but it may be reduced to a maximum of 10 years. The duration may be extended for a period of up to 20 years, or reduced to 5 years, depending on the case.
EU countries may require that the certificate be subject to the payment of annual fees. The annual fees are to be paid by the applicant or by the holder.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2007 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Protected medicinal products’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Patent: a patent granted by an EU country to a person or a company for the purpose of preventing, limiting or limiting the supply of a substance or a service to a particular population or to a specific group of persons or groups of persons, or to the general public.

Summary 178:
Convention on jurisdiction and enforcement of judgments in civil and commercial matters (Switzerland-EC Convention)
Contribution to the conclusion of the Convention on Jurisdiction and Enforcement of Judgments in Civil and Commercial Matters (SICC Convention) by the European Community and the European Free Trade Association (Euratom)
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2016/852 concluding the Convention relating to jurisdiction and the recognition and enforcement by the EU of the International Convention on the jurisdiction and Enforcement by the International Court of Justice of the Swiss Confederation
Convention relating to the jurisdiction of the European Convention on Judgement and Enforcement in Civil And Commercial Matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to ensure that judgments are recognised and enforced in all EU countries.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
The parties to the convention are Switzerland, the EU, the European Economic Community (EFTA), the European Atomic Energy Community (EEA), the EU countries, the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland (1), Ireland, the Republic of Ireland, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland, Sweden, Switzerland and the United States of America (1).
The aim of the convention is to:
ensure that judgments issued by EU countries are recognised by the courts of the other contracting parties;
promote the free movement of persons, goods and services within the EU;
protect intellectual property rights;
facilitate access to justice and the protection of intellectual property;
improve cooperation between the contracting parties in the fight against counterfeiting and counterfeiting;
strengthen promote the application of the principle of non-discrimination between the EU and non-EU countries;
contribute to the harmonisation of laws, regulations and administrative procedures in the area of jurisdiction;
encourage cooperation between EU countries in the field of competition;
support the development of a free trade area between the signatory countries and the EU as a whole.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
 
The EU has ratified the convention and entered into force on 1 July 2016.
BACKGROUND
The Convention on Justice and Enforcement is one of a series of legal instruments designed to ensure the effective application of EU law.
For more information, see:
‘Judgment and enforcement’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Judgement: a decision by a court of an EU country to enforce a judgment.
ACT
Council Decision 2006/856/EC of 29 June 2006 on the conclusion, on behalf the European Union, of the Convention relating on jurisdiction, and on the recognition, enforcement and enforcement in civil & commercial matters between the European Communities and the International Courts of Justice (OJ C 202, 1.7.2006, pp. 1-8)
RELATED ACTS
Regulation (EC) No 44/2001 of the EC Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2001 on the application by the Member States of the Treaty on European Union of the Protocol to the Accession of the Community to the Convention concerning the jurisdiction, recognition and enforceability of judgments, and amending the Protocol on the Recognition, Enforcement and Approximation of Civil & Commercial Jurisdictions (Codified version).
